### Question 2: Can you differentiate a cross-listed course and elective applied course in the case of a double major?  
### Answer: 

In the context provided, a cross-listed course refers to courses that are shared between majors or between a major and a minor, and are typically tagged by these programs. These courses can be used to satisfy requirements for multiple programs, up to a maximum of 8 credits per pair of programs.

An elective applied course, on the other hand, is not specifically defined in the given text. Generally, electives are courses chosen by the student outside of required courses, while applied courses might refer to practical or real-world application-focused courses. Without specific definitions from the text, it's not possible to differentiate an elective applied course from a cross-listed course in this context. Therefore, in the case of a double major, a student would need to consult with their academic advisor to determine how to apply courses towards their requirements. 

The text does not provide clear differentiation between cross-listed courses and elective applied courses, so any distinction would depend on the specific policies and definitions used by the institution.

This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. ### Question 3: I would like to ask for the capstone withdrawal policy. What will be the impact when I choose to drop the capstone before the Fall 2025 term starts? Will there be any penalties associated with withdrawing, such as a 'W' notation on my transcript?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided context, the capstone withdrawal policy does not specifically address withdrawal before the Fall 2025 term starts. However, generally speaking, for courses other than the capstone, attempting to withdraw during the first period (Week 2 to Week 4) allows a student to do so without any consequences, and no "W" grade will be recorded on the transcript. 

For the capstone, the policy states that a student should first discuss the matter with the primary advisor and the grading committee. If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within three business days of receiving the final grade (P/F/H).

There is no specific mention of penalties or a 'W' notation for withdrawing from the capstone before the term starts. Therefore, it is advisable to consult with your academic advisor regarding the specific procedures and potential impacts of withdrawing from the capstone before the term begins. The context does not provide explicit information about penalties or 'W' notations for capstone withdrawals prior to the term start.

### Question 4: Questions related to course history, in which one course can have multiple IDs? Like Advanced Deep Learning course. How would it be handled among different cohorts?  
### Answer: 

When a course like Advanced Deep Learning has multiple IDs and is offered to different cohorts, it typically means that the course content may evolve over time due to updates, improvements, or changes in the curriculum. Here's how it could be handled:

1. **Course Versioning**: Each version of the course could be assigned a unique ID. For example, the first offering might be Course ID 12345, the second might be Course ID 12346, and so on. This way, each cohort would be enrolled in a specific version of the course.

2. **Cohort-Specific Content**: Different cohorts might receive slightly different content depending on when they enroll. For instance, newer versions of the course might include updated materials, new case studies, or additional resources that weren't available in earlier versions.

3. **Consistent Core Material**: While there might be variations between versions, the core material and learning objectives would likely remain consistent across all versions. This ensures that students from different cohorts are learning the same fundamental concepts.

4. **Backward Compatibility**: If possible, older versions of the course might still be accessible for students who started before the course was updated. However, they would not receive any new content or updates.

5. **Communication with Students**: The institution would need to clearly communicate to students about the differences between versions of the course. This includes informing them about what new content they will receive and how it differs from previous versions.

By implementing these strategies, institutions can manage courses with multiple IDs effectively, ensuring that each cohort receives appropriate and relevant instruction while maintaining consistency in core learning outcomes.

### Question 5: I have taken Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis in Fall 2023. Am I eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you are eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024. According to the provided information, advanced level courses in Economics can be taken after completing at least one of Microeconomic and Macroeconomic Analysis and Econometrics. Since you have already taken Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis, you meet the prerequisite for advanced level courses like Financial Economics. However, please note that you might also need to have completed Econometrics depending on the specific course requirements. It's advisable to check the course syllabus or consult with the Economics major coordinator for any updates or additional requirements.

Courses: Principles of Economics 1 and 2 (100-level) These two courses introduce microeconomics and macroeconomics, providing an overview of economic theories and analytical techniques applied to current issues. By studying both microeconomics (the analysis of choices made by people, firms, and governments) and macroeconomics (the analysis of the economy as a whole) students will develop their economic intuition as they better understand the functioning of the world. Methodology Courses: Economic Methods (100-level) This course introduces basic concepts and methods of statistical analysis and fundamental rules of mathematics used in economic analysis. ### Question 6: If I have waived the course Computer Science I, but I want to declare Computer Science major, do I have to take Computer Science I?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you have to take Computer Science I to declare Computer Science as your major. Waiving the course does not exempt you from this requirement. According to the provided information, "To formally declare Computer Science as their major, the student must complete at least two Computer Science courses (MATH 202 - Discrete Math is also counted)." Since Computer Science I is a foundational course required for the major, it cannot be waived if you wish to officially declare Computer Science as your major. Therefore, you need to take Computer Science I to meet the major requirements.

### Question 7: If I have taken the following courses: Mathematical Statistics, Abstract Algebra, Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, Calculus, Differential Equation, Stochastic Calculus, Statistical Learning, Discrete Mathematics, Probability, am I eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics? What about majoring in Applied Mathematics?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you are eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics. You have taken at least 6 Mathematics courses, including at least 1 Advanced course (Mathematical Statistics, Stochastic Calculus, Statistical Learning) and 2 Intermediate courses (Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, Differential Equation, Probability, Discrete Mathematics).

However, you are not eligible to major in Applied Mathematics because you have not taken any Foundation courses. The requirements for declaring an Applied Mathematics major state that students need to complete at least 2 Foundation courses or 1 Foundation and 1 Intermediate course. Since you have not taken any Foundation courses, you do not meet the requirements for declaring a major in Applied Mathematics. 

Additionally, you have taken more than the required number of Intermediate courses, which is good, but it does not compensate for the lack of Foundation courses. Therefore, you cannot major in Applied Mathematics at this time. However, you can still pursue a minor in Applied Mathematics. 

Please consult with an academic advisor to confirm your eligibility and plan your coursework accordingly.

Therefore, you need to ensure that all 100-level major requirements are fulfilled before applying for the Capstone. Additionally, you must maintain a minimum major GPA of 3.6 and have your proposal approved by the major faculty. If these criteria are met, you would be eligible to start a Capstone in Arts and Media Studies. Please consult with your prospective advisor to confirm the status of your major requirements and discuss your Capstone proposal.

1.  General Information: 1.1. Description In masonry, the “capstone” is the stone that sits on top of, or “caps” an arch, wall, or other structure, giving it a polished appearance while demonstrating the strength of the underlying structure. Similarly, the senior Capstone project is intended to “cap off” your undergraduate education with a polished piece of original research that demonstrates your mastery of particular skills and knowledge—in this case, historical reasoning on a subject of your choosing. The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]

The main role of your Capstone advisor is to guide you through the research process and to evaluate your mastery of that process, regardless of the topic. ### Question 10: Given I have finished these subjects: Advanced Deep Learning, Machine Learning, Deep Learning, Database. Are they sufficient for the Advanced Courses requirement of the computer science major?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, it seems that you have completed some relevant courses but not all that are typically required for the Advanced Courses requirement in the computer science major.

The courses you have completed are:
- Advanced Deep Learning
- Machine Learning
- Deep Learning
- Database Systems

The courses listed under "Advanced Courses" in the context provided are:
- CS310: Web Applications & Human-Computer Interaction
- CS311: Advanced Deep Learning
- CS312: Natural Language Processing
- CS313: Deep Learning for AI

You have already completed CS311 (Advanced Deep Learning), which is one of the advanced courses. However, you still need to complete the following courses to meet the Advanced Courses requirement:
- CS310: Web Applications & Human-Computer Interaction
- CS312: Natural Language Processing
- CS313: Deep Learning for AI

Additionally, you may need to ensure that you have completed any prerequisites for these courses, such as CS201, MATH103, or other foundational courses mentioned in the context.

Therefore, while you have completed one advanced course, you still need to complete three more to fulfill the Advanced Courses requirement for the computer science major. It's advisable to check the official curriculum requirements for your specific program to confirm the exact courses needed.

### Question 11: I have a question if I take a gap year, will my financial aid be canceled? If yes, can I still re-apply for the financial aid program when I get back to school?  
### Answer: 

If you take a gap year, your financial aid is not necessarily canceled. However, you must reapply for financial aid when you return to Fulbright. According to the information provided, "Students who wish to return to Fulbright after withdrawing formally or without permission must reapply for admission and financial aid." Therefore, you would need to reapply for financial aid upon your return. Your previous financial aid status does not automatically continue after a gap year. It's important to follow the procedures outlined for re-admission and financial aid application to ensure you receive the necessary support when you return to Fulbright.

If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. After one term of Admin LOA, a student is officially withdrawn from Fulbright unless they have contacted the Registrar’s Office and confirmed the plan to return by registering for course(s) or have been granted a leave extension, a maximum of another term. The extension must be endorsed by the Registrar’s Office and approved by the Dean’s Office.

While on suspension, a student may not visit the Fulbright campus unless permission is given from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions typically are for one term or one academic year. A student may be suspended a maximum of two times. A student will not be suspended a third time but will instead have their enrolment in the program canceled. A student in this situation must apply for re-admission. The student must include with his or her application for re-admission a letter that addresses the reasons for their suspensions and cancellation, and the measures they have taken to address those reasons. ### Question 13: If I major in Economics, is it sufficient that I take Scholar Development to fulfill Experiential Learning requirements?  
### Answer: 

No, taking Scholar Development alone is not sufficient to fulfill the Experiential Learning requirements. According to the information provided, all full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students must complete at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement. The ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), and each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). Therefore, simply taking Scholar Development would not meet the comprehensive experiential learning requirements. You need to participate in various ELP streams offered by these teams to accumulate the required credits.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation

For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. ### Question 14: Is it sufficient for me to complete 4 credits in EL if I major in Engineering?  
### Answer: 

No, it is not sufficient to complete only 4 credits in EL if you major in Engineering. According to the information provided, all full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students must complete at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement for the Engineering major. Therefore, completing just 4 credits would not meet the minimum requirement.

### Question 15: Can I take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses?  
### Answer: 

It is possible to take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses, but it would depend on the specific requirements of the engineering program you are enrolled in. Generally, the statement mentions that these courses are accessible to undetermined-major students to pursue courses of interest, but the exact number of intermediate courses required might vary. Therefore, you should check the official curriculum guidelines for your specific program to confirm the exact requirements.

<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 46]
been exposed to understanding the users' needs, defining engineering problems, and ideating potential solutions before gaining some hands-on experience creating, making, and testing a physical product. Students interested in exploring further can take several Foundation Engineering courses, which are designed specifically to bridge engineering practice, mathematics, and basic sciences. In general, these courses only require the core engineering course as the prerequisite, if any, making them accessible to undetermined-major students to pursue courses of interest. Once the students declare their major or minor in Engineering, they will gain more specialized knowledge and skills by taking more Engineering Foundation courses and Engineering Advanced courses. As part of a human-centered approach that aims to determine human-centric problems and then apply innovative engineering solutions, the students will be encouraged to take Elective courses in Arts, Humanities, Social Sciences, and Entrepreneurship. The Advanced-level courses and two-semester Capstone projects provide students with deep knowledge and a chance to apply what they have learned into real-world problems. In addition, students must complete a well-balanced set of courses in mathematics, natural sciences, arts, humanities, and social sciences to be awarded a bachelor's degree in engineering. Although students will be required to take half of the minimum number of credits for graduation in engineering, they will have a certain degree of freedom of choosing   elective courses to pursue their interest of study with engineering. ### Question 16: If I have completed the course Intro to AI, will CS207 - Object-Oriented Analysis and Design and CS211 – Operating Systems suffice to fill the rest two intermediate courses?  
### Answer: 

No, CS207 - Object-Oriented Analysis and Design and CS211 – Operating Systems alone will not suffice to fill the rest two intermediate courses.

The reasoning behind this answer is that the context provided specifies that Integrated Sciences students are required to complete one course in Statistics and one course in Programming. It also mentions that any 100-level and 200-level course related to Statistics and Programming can be taken to fulfill this requirement. However, CS207 and CS211 are not listed as courses that fulfill the Statistics or Programming requirement. Therefore, completing these courses would not meet the requirement for the Integrated Sciences major. 

Additionally, the context does not mention that CS207 and CS211 can substitute for the Statistics and Programming courses needed for the Integrated Sciences major. Thus, these courses cannot be used to fulfill the requirement for the Integrated Sciences major. Hence, the answer is no.

### Question 17: Does completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfy the core theory requirement, or is an additional course needed?  
### Answer: 

Completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfies the core theory requirement. An additional course is not needed according to the information provided.

### Question 18: If I want to major in Engineering, can I choose other programming courses besides Computer Science I and Computer Science II, for instance Introduction to data visualization?  
### Answer: 

If you're majoring in Engineering, you might be able to choose other programming courses like Introduction to Data Visualization, but it depends on your specific program's requirements and whether the course is cross-listed with Computer Science or approved as an elective. It's best to check with your academic advisor to ensure the course fits your major's requirements. Otherwise, Computer Science I and Computer Science II are typically required for Computer Science majors, not necessarily for Engineering majors. Therefore, you should focus on courses that align with the Engineering major's prerequisites and electives.

### Question 19: Given I took Discrete Mathematics in Spring 2022 and earned B, then the same course in Spring 2024 and earned C-, which grades will be kept?  
### Answer: 

The higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. Therefore, the B grade from Spring 2022 will be kept. The C- grade from Spring 2024 will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 2]
GRADING .......................................................................................................................... 6: 4.1 Repeating Courses ............................................................................................................................................ 8 4.2 Final Grade Release .......................................................................................................................................... 8 4.3 Credit Transfer and Exemptions earned from other universities. .............................................. 8

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
students’ request. 4.1 Repeating Courses Students are required to repeat core courses in the case of receiving the grade F and/or course(s) counted toward major/minor in the case of receiving a grade below ‘C-’. Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a ‘D+’ following consultation with the student’s academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. ### Question 20: Can I register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4. The context specifies that no course can be taken to fulfill more than one category, and typically, exploratory courses are limited to 100-level or 200-level courses. Therefore, 300-level courses do not meet the requirement for exploratory courses.

### Question 21: Can I register for more than 20 credits in a semester?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register for more than 20 credits in a semester without submitting the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office and obtaining approval from your Academic/Major Advisor.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office. ### Question 22: What is the maximum number of times I can retake a course to improve my grade, and how does it affect my transcript?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided information, a student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet major requirements. If a student repeats a course, the higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and will remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. Therefore, the maximum number of times a student can retake a course to improve their grade is two, unless specific conditions are met. After the second attempt, the course cannot be retaken without meeting the specified conditions.

### Question 23: For a student doing the literature capstone, if a student includes charts or tables, do they count toward the word limit?  
### Answer: 

Charts or tables do not count toward the word limit according to the guidelines provided. The word count regulations state that submissions should be between 10,000-15,000 words, excluding full bibliography and images with captions. Therefore, charts and tables would be considered images with captions and thus do not contribute to the word count.

### Question 24: If I failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, can I redo it in Spring 2025?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, if you failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, you would typically be required to repeat the course. According to the context, students are required to repeat core courses in the case of receiving a grade of 'F'. Therefore, you would need to take Capstone I again, likely in the Spring 2025 semester, to have another opportunity to pass the course. The higher grade you achieve will be used in your GPA calculation, and the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP" (repeated) and remain on your transcript. However, please note that course availability and capacity should also be considered when planning to retake the course. It's advisable to consult with your academic advisor and the Registrar's Office for specific guidance regarding your situation.

### Question 25: If I do Literature capstone in Decolonial studies, can it be approved?  
### Answer: 

Yes, it can be approved as long as there is faculty expertise in the field of decolonial studies. The Literature Program includes expertise in postcolonial studies, which is closely related to decolonial studies. Therefore, if a faculty member with expertise in postcolonial studies is available, your capstone project in decolonial studies would likely be approved. However, if there is no faculty expertise in decolonial studies, the project may not be approved. It's recommended to consult with prospective advisors early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project.

### Question 26: I am a Co24 majoring in Computer Science and taking the Database course. Does it count as major courses?  
### Answer: 

No, the Database course does not explicitly count as a major course in the provided information. Based on the major outline, the required courses include CS 101, CS 201, CS 203, MATH 202, three intermediate courses, CS 302, four advanced courses, and capstone courses. The Database course (CS304) is listed under electives, suggesting it is optional and not part of the core major requirements. Therefore, while it is related to your field of study, it does not count towards fulfilling the major requirements for Computer Science. Please consult with your academic advisor for confirmation.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

### Question 27: Can Discrete Mathematics be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors?  
### Answer: 

Yes, Discrete Mathematics (MATH 202) can be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors. It is part of the core requirements for Computer Science and can also be considered as a Pure Mathematics course for the Applied Mathematics major. However, it should be noted that the specific requirements for each major might have additional constraints or recommendations regarding course overlap. Therefore, students should consult the respective major requirements for detailed guidance.

Pure Mathematics courses: These courses provide the essential abstract concepts and structures that connect various branches of Mathematics and help students understand the adaptability of Mathematics to different types of problems. Students are required to take at least 1 Pure mathematics course. Sample Pure mathematics courses • Abstract Algebra • Real Analysis Research seminars: The seminars provide chances for students to understand about faculty’s research as well as recent developments in mathematical research. Students will also practice basic research skills such as finding resources, writing literature review, and identifying research methodology. Capstone project (optional): This is a one-year long research project to be completed in the last year of study. The project deliverable is either a research paper or a product which contributes to the knowledge of mathematics or its applications. ### Question 28: What steps should I take to ensure a smooth transfer of my exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

To ensure a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright, you should follow these steps:

1. Review the Transfer Credit Policy V1.0 published in the One-Stop portal to understand the process and requirements.

2. Gather all necessary information about the courses you want to transfer, including course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

3. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer to the Office of the Registrar at Fulbright University Vietnam. Make sure to send the official transcript with seal from Bard College directly to the Office of the Registrar at the email registrar@fulbright.edu.vn or the mailing address provided in the policy.

4. Consult with your Academic/Major Advisor at Fulbright to discuss your program plan and ensure that the transferred credits align with your degree requirements.

5. Keep track of any deadlines or requirements for submitting the application and supporting documents.

By following these steps, you can help ensure a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright. Remember to provide accurate and complete information to facilitate the evaluation process.

<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 29: Are 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement?  
### Answer: 

Yes, 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 are also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement. According to the context provided, students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. This implies that only courses explicitly categorized under these three categories are eligible for fulfilling the Exploratory requirement. Courses not categorized as such do not count towards this requirement.

Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. ### Question 31: If I withdraw from a course after the 4th week of the semester, will I be deducted 4 credits of financial aid?  
### Answer: 

No, you will not be deducted 4 credits of financial aid. Withdrawing from a course after the 4th week of the semester will result in a grade of 'F', which affects your GPA, but it does not directly affect your financial aid eligibility in terms of credit deductions. However, if your total credits fall below the minimum for full-time enrollment (typically 12 credits), it could impact your financial aid. Always consult with your financial aid office for specific guidance.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. Exceptions will only be permitted in exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits.  Students should be aware that course withdrawals may

The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. ### Question 32: Why do I need to take 8 exploratory courses?  
### Answer: 

You need to take 8 exploratory courses to step out of your comfort zone and explore broad areas of study. This helps you discover more fully where your interests and passions lie. These courses are divided into three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. Each category requires you to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level). No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. Up to two of these 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. For Class of 2024, 2025, 2026, and 2027 students, there are four exploratory categories: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing. Class of 2024 students need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulfill their Exploratory requirements, one course from each category, with at most 4 out of 16 credits counted as Pass/No Pass. Students of classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027 need to complete 32 credits (8 courses), eight credits from each category, to fulfill their Exploratory requirements. The goal is to help students broaden their knowledge and find their academic interests.

### Question 33: Can I take 160 credits in 4 years given that I pay for the full tuition fee?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you cannot take 160 credits in 4 years. The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term, and students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Therefore, the maximum number of credits you could accumulate over 4 years would be 80 credits, assuming you take the maximum course load every term. To graduate, you need to earn a minimum of 128 credit hours, so taking 160 credits exceeds the minimum requirement but is still within the typical range for a full-time student's course load. However, the question specifically asks about 160 credits in 4 years, which is not possible given the constraints mentioned. Therefore, you cannot take 160 credits in 4 years under these conditions. The payment of full tuition fees does not change this limitation on the number of credits you can take.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours.  The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 34: What are the requirements for mathematics courses to pursue Human-Centered Engineering major?  
### Answer: 

To pursue the Human-Centered Engineering major, students are required to take at least 1 Pure Mathematics course. This requirement ensures that students gain essential abstract concepts and structures that connect various branches of Mathematics and help them understand the adaptability of Mathematics to different types of problems. Additionally, students need to complete 2 intermediate courses, 2 advanced courses in specialized areas of study, and 2 elective applied courses approved by the major coordinator (at least one at the 200 level). These courses contribute to developing necessary skills for working well in a multidisciplinary team and applying innovative engineering solutions to human-centric problems. The sample courses provided include topics like Abstract Algebra, Real Analysis, Signal, Systems, and Control, Computer Vision, and others, which align with the requirements for the major. It's important to note that students cannot double-count a course for two different requirements, such as Operations Research, which can only count for either 1 Advanced course or 1 Elective course. Pure Mathematics courses are specifically mentioned as a requirement for this major.

In general, these courses only require the core engineering course as the prerequisite, if any, making them accessible to undetermined-major students to pursue courses of interest. Once the students declare their major or minor in Engineering, they will gain more specialized knowledge and skills by taking more Engineering Foundation courses and Engineering Advanced courses. As part of a human-centered approach that aims to determine human-centric problems and then apply innovative engineering solutions, the students will be encouraged to take Elective courses in Arts, Humanities, Social Sciences, and Entrepreneurship. ### Question 35: How is the grade of a replaced course displayed on the transcript? Will it replace the old one or create a new entry in the transcript?  
### Answer: 

The grade of a replaced course will be displayed on the transcript such that the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. The higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation but will not create a new entry; instead, it will overwrite the previous grade. Therefore, the transcript will show the "RP" notation alongside the higher grade, indicating that the course was repeated.  

<details>

advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. ### Question 36: What are the courses that can replace the capstone for a given major?  
### Answer: 

There are no courses that can replace the capstone for a given major according to the provided context. The capstone is specifically defined as a culmination of the student's curriculum demonstrating principal learning outcomes and competencies, and it must be completed as a written thesis in the Computer Science major. Therefore, no other courses can fulfill this requirement.

What is a capstone in Computer Science?: According to university-wide policy, the capstone is a culmination to the student’s curriculum to demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. In the Computer Science major, the capstone is an individual project and can take only the form of a written thesis. The capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. You should think very carefully about an appropriate scope of research and production for your proposed capstone. Keep in mind that projects for which there is no current faculty expertise may not be approved. It is important for you to consult early on with your potential advisor to ensure the matchs. Applications which do not demonstrate awareness of the scope and the practicalities needed to realize the capstone may not be approved. ### Question 37: Is it possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics? If yes, please provide a sample study plan.  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics. However, students must ensure that they do not double count courses for two different requirements.

Sample Study Plan:
1. General education courses (Core and Exploratory, as required by Undergraduate curriculum), of which up to two Exploratory courses (8 credits) can be counted towards the major.
2. Experiential Learning (4 – 12 credits).
3. Required foundation courses: Linear Algebra, Calculus, Introduction to Statistics, Multivariable Calculus (16 credits).
4. 1 writing course (Ideas in Mathematics/Advanced Mathematical Writing) (4 credits).
5. 2 intermediate courses (8 credits).
6. 1 Pure Mathematics course (4 credits).
7. 2 advanced courses in specialized areas of study (8 credits).
8. 2 elective applied courses approved by the major coordinator (at least one at 200 level) (8 credits).
9. Research seminar (4 credits)
10. Capstone I and Capstone II (8 credits) for Honors program.
11. OR 2 advanced courses in Human-Centered Engineering (8 credits).

Additionally, students should choose courses from the following samples:
Applied Mathematics Courses: Operations Research, Introduction to Quantitative Finance
Human-Centered Engineering Courses: Engineering Exploration: Sink or Swim, Signal, Systems, and Control, Computer Vision

Students should also take relevant courses in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics to fulfill the requirements for both majors. They should consult with advisors to ensure that they are meeting all requirements for both majors and avoiding double counting courses. The exact schedule may vary depending on the specific requirements of each major.

Students should be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if resulting in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. • Waitlist: Each course at Fulbright has a maximum capacity. The registration system on the Fulbright One Stop portal allows students to join a waitlist for courses that are full. Should space become available, students will be enrolled in the course in order of their appearance on the waitlist during the registration or Add/Drop time. When a waitlisted student is added to a course, it is the

### Question 39: What are the exchange policies of Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

The exchange policies of Fulbright involve students applying for Credit Transfer or an Exemption for courses taken at other universities. A student can transfer up to 64 credit hours to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree. To apply, the student must provide detailed information about the course(s) including curriculum, learning outcomes, content, and assessments. The application is submitted to the Office of the Registrar, who then coordinates with the Office of the Dean to decide on the credit transfer or exemption. The policies are subject to regular updates as the university continues to innovate and improve. There is also a specific policy for AP/IB/CIE courses which is currently under development. For more detailed information, students should refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 available on the One Stop portal.

### Question 40: What actions are considered plagiarism? Are AI-generated works counted?  
### Answer: 

Actions considered plagiarism typically involve presenting someone else's work or ideas as your own without proper citation or acknowledgment. This includes copying text, ideas, images, or other forms of content without giving credit to the original creator.

Regarding AI-generated works, they are indeed considered part of the creative process and can be counted, but they need to be properly documented and acknowledged. According to the guidelines provided, creative projects involving generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should clearly define the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the specific elements of the project it contributes to, specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed, outline how AI will be incorporated, address ethical and copyright concerns, and highlight the originality and human contributions to the project. By doing so, students ensure transparency and offer insight into the role of AI in the creative process. Therefore, AI-generated works can be counted as long as they are properly documented and acknowledged according to the specified guidelines.

<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]

Creative projects involving generative AI will require full documentation of its usage. Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include: • Objective and Scope: Clearly deﬁne the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the speciﬁc elements of the project it contributes to. • Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed. • Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI. • Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout

### Question 41: Why is the graduation requirement 128 credits, but the major requirement is only 48 credits?  
### Answer: 

The graduation requirement is 128 credits because it includes all the courses needed to fulfill general education, electives, and other non-major specific requirements. The major requirement is only 48 credits because it only accounts for the courses directly related to the major field of study. The difference between the two reflects the broader scope of a college education compared to the focus on a single major.

### Question 42: Explain the cross-listed mechanism between courses.  
### Answer: 

The cross-listed mechanism allows students to use up to 8 credits (two courses) from one major to satisfy the requirements of another major or minor, provided that the courses are cross-listed or tagged. This limit applies per each pair of majors (or major and minor). For instance, a student majoring in both A and B and minoring in C could use 2 courses from A and B, 2 from B and C, and 2 from A and C, totaling 6 double-counted courses. However, this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. Courses required for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major but not cross-listed do not count toward the 8-credit limit. Interdisciplinary minors also have courses that are not cross-listed and are referred to as 'tagged'. These courses cannot be used to satisfy the 8-credit limit. The mechanism aims to allow flexibility in fulfilling requirements across different programs while maintaining academic standards.  

<details>

### Question 44: How does the core quest course selection work to fulfill core credits?  
### Answer: 

The core quest course selection works to fulfill core credits by preassigning students in their first year or the first semester of the second year to four specific courses within the QUEST (Quantitative Understanding and Empirical Scientific Thinking) group. These courses are: Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age (4 credits), Scientific Inquiry (4 credits), Introduction to Statistics (4 credits), and Programming for Data Science and Visualization (4 credits). These courses are designed to meet the quantitative reasoning and scientific inquiry requirements of the core curriculum. Students do not have the option to choose these courses themselves but are required to complete all four as part of their core curriculum. This ensures that all students receive a standardized foundation in quantitative and scientific thinking early in their academic program. After completing these core quest courses, students then proceed to fulfill their exploratory requirements and major-specific coursework.

### Question 45: Can I take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement. The context states that advanced level courses (300-level) can only be taken after completing specific prerequisite courses such as Microeconomic and Macroeconomic Analysis and Econometrics. Therefore, a 300-level course would not be suitable to fulfill a 200-level requirement.

### Question 46: If I take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn’t have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, can I count it toward that major?  
### Answer: 

If you take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn't have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, you might still be able to count it toward that major. However, the course would need to be "tagged" by the relevant major or minor at Fulbright. This means that even though the course isn't directly cross-listed, it can still count towards the major's requirements if it meets the learning outcomes and content expectations of the Fulbright course it is tagging. It's important to provide detailed information about the course, including its curriculum, learning outcomes, content, and assessments, to the Office of the Registrar for evaluation. They will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine if the course can be counted towards the major requirements. Keep in mind that there are limitations on how many courses can be counted this way, and each course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements to avoid triple counting. Always consult with your Academic/Major Advisor to ensure the course fits into your program plan.

### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you need at least 128 credit hours to graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright. You currently have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL, which totals 128 credits. Therefore, you have met the minimum credit hour requirement to potentially graduate. However, it's important to ensure that these credits cover all the necessary requirements for your specific degree program, including any experiential learning credits. Consult with your Academic/Major Advisor to confirm that you have fulfilled all graduation requirements.

### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you cannot take only 2 courses in a regular term if you want to maintain full-time enrollment status. Full-time enrollment typically requires registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term.

If you are unable to take a full course load due to exceptional circumstances such as illness or medical conditions, you would need to provide a letter from a licensed medical doctor detailing your situation, including how it affects your ability to study, the treatment plan, and when you might be able to return to full-time studies. If approved, you might be eligible for tuition credit, but no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits.

It's important to note that course withdrawals may also impact your financial aid eligibility if they result in fewer than the minimum credits required for full-time enrollment. Therefore, you should consult with your academic advisor and the Registrar's Office to explore your options and ensure you understand the implications of reducing your course load. 

In summary, taking only 2 courses is not typical for a regular term, and it could affect both your academic progress and financial aid. You should seek approval under exceptional circumstances and follow the procedures outlined for such situations.

### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

According to the information provided, you can major in multiple subjects, including three majors. However, it's specified that students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. The text does not explicitly state a limitation on the number of majors a student can pursue, but it does emphasize that each major's requirements must be fully completed. Therefore, while there is no explicit restriction to three majors, the practicality and workload involved in completing the requirements for three different majors would be significant. It is advisable to consult with an academic advisor to ensure feasibility and to understand the implications of such a decision.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard duration. In other words, students have a maximum of 8 years to complete their studies.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

The process of delaying your payment involves contacting the Student Financial Services team to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing you in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from you. This allows them to understand your situation and potentially provide assistance or alternative solutions. However, it's important to note that after the approved period of absence, you will be put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if there is no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. After one term of Admin LOA, you will be officially withdrawn from Fulbright unless you have contacted the Registrar’s Office and confirmed the plan to return by registering for course(s) or have been granted a leave extension, a maximum of another term. The extension must be endorsed by the Registrar’s Office and approved by the Dean’s Office. If you anticipate being unable to clear the account on time, you should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. Remember, the goal is to ensure that you can continue your studies without interruption.  

<details>

### Question 58: How can I audit a course?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided in the context, there is no explicit mention of auditing a course. The form appears to be related to requesting approval to take a course on a Pass/No Pass basis, not auditing. Therefore, the references in the form are irrelevant to the question about auditing a course. To audit a course, you would typically need to check with your institution's specific policies and procedures, as auditing options and requirements vary between institutions. Generally, auditing a course does not involve earning credit or a grade, but it allows you to attend lectures and participate in class activities without the obligation to complete assignments or exams. However, for precise details, you should contact your academic advisor or the registrar's office at your institution.

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

If you're going for a double major, the maximum number of courses that can be double-counted is 8 credits (2 courses) per pair of majors. This means for two majors, you can double-count up to 8 credits. However, you must complete all requirements for each major. The rule about double-counting applies per pair of majors and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits across all your majors. So, for a double major, you can potentially double-count up to 8 credits for each major combination you have.

### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

The grade translation from alphabetic to numerical at Fulbright University is as follows:

- A-: 3.7
- B+: 3.3

Grades from 'A' to 'B-' and 'C+' to 'F' would fall between these two points, but their exact values are not specified in the provided information. For example, an 'A' could be 4.0, 'B' could be around 3.0, and so on. However, without specific values for those grades, we can only provide the translation for A- and B+. 

Additionally, any grade below 'C-' is considered a No Pass (NP) and does not grant credit. Grades of 'C-' or higher are counted as a Pass. 

Please note that the exact numerical values for other grades might vary depending on the specific policies set by the faculty for individual courses. The registrar's office handles the conversion to P/NP after the final grades are submitted by instructors. 

If you need more precise values for other grades, you should refer to the official university guidelines or consult the faculty for each course. 

For incomplete grades (I), they are temporary and must be completed within 6 months; otherwise, they convert to NP. 

This information is based on the grading system described in the document provided. If there are any discrepancies or additional details, it would be best to check the official university handbook or contact the registrar's office directly.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you failed to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. Typically, this results in an updated Learning Contract and lasts for a term. If you do not meet the conditions set by the Dean’s Office, you may be placed on Academic Suspension. Suspensions are entered on your transcript and you must meet with the Dean’s Office to establish the conditions you need to meet before returning to Fulbright. While on suspension, you may not visit the Fulbright campus without permission from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions are typically for one term or one academic year, and you may be suspended a maximum of two times. If you are suspended a third time, your enrollment in the program will be canceled, and you will need to apply for re-admission. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. You must also re-apply for financial aid.

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP (Pass/No Pass) grading system works as follows:

1. **Eligibility**: Students can take up to 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) per academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. This decision must be made by completing a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submitting it to the Registrar's Office before 4:00 PM on Friday of Week 4 of the term.

2. **Conversion Process**: The Registrar's Office is responsible for converting the final grade submitted by the instructor at the end of the term into either a Pass (P) or No Pass (NP).

3. **Grading Criteria**:
   - A grade of 'C-' or higher is considered a Pass.
   - Any grade below a 'C-' is considered a No Pass (NP).

4. **Credit and Prerequisite Requirements**: 
   - Courses graded with a Pass can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.
   - Courses with a No Pass grade (NP) cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses and do not grant any credit.

5. **Irreversible Decision**: Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back.

6. **Core Courses**: Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

7. **Incomplete Grades**: If a student is unable to complete the course due to exceptional circumstances, an incomplete grade ('I') may be given temporarily. The student must complete the remaining coursework within 6 months; otherwise, the grade defaults to a No Pass (NP).

This system allows students to focus on passing courses without the pressure of earning specific letter grades, but it comes with limitations regarding credit and prerequisite usage.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 2 courses on a Pass/No Pass (P/NP) basis in one academic year. These courses typically amount to 8 credits in total. 

Courses graded with a Pass (P) will be counted towards your prerequisite requirements but will not contribute to your official transcript GPA. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass (NP) and will not grant credit, thus not contributing to your GPA either. Therefore, while these courses can help you meet prerequisites, they do not affect your GPA calculation. The grades for these P/NP courses will appear on your Official Transcript as either 'P' or 'NP'. 

It's important to note that core courses cannot be taken on a P/NP basis and do not contribute to your major/minor requirements. Once a course is converted to P/NP, the grade option cannot be changed back. This means that if you choose to take a course on a P/NP basis, you are committed to that grading option for that course.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

No, the grade of 'No Pass' (NP) will not be counted towards the 144 maximum credits you can have. According to the context provided, "Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result." Therefore, the NP grade does not contribute to your total credit count. However, it's important to note that courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Make sure to discuss your situation with your academic advisor to explore potential options or accommodations.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

To receive an Academic Warning, students who are not making satisfactory progress towards their degree, fall below a 2.0 GPA, or face issues related to attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity are typically notified. An Academic Warning is issued by the Registrar’s Office. The student must then attend an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract is created, outlining specific conditions tailored to the student's situation. The Registrar's Office records this information and follows up accordingly. If a student receives three official warnings, it could lead to more severe disciplinary actions like Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. This process aims to help students improve their academic performance and stay on track for degree completion.

### Question 67: How can I make reservations of rooms for personal usage?

There is no information provided in the given context regarding making reservations for rooms for personal usage. The text focuses on exit checklists and procedures for leaving Fulbright, but does not mention room reservation policies. Therefore, the references are irrelevant to the question.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided information, here are some suggested courses to major in Math:

Foundation Courses:
- Linear Algebra
- Single Variable Calculus
- Introduction to Statistics
- Multivariable Calculus

Intermediate Courses:
- Probability
- Differential Equations
- Discrete Mathematics
- Numerical Analysis

Advanced Courses:
- Advanced Statistics
- Statistical Learning
- Stochastic Calculus
- Numerical Analysis
- Optimization
- Partial Differential Equations

Elective Applied Courses:
- Game Theory
- The Economics of Corruption
- Money and Banking
- Economics of Inequality
- Economics of Education
- Cost-Benefit Analysis
- Market Design
- Signal, Systems, and Control
- Computer Vision
- Introduction to Machine Learning
- Algorithm
- Statistical Learning
- Introduction to AI
- Operations Research
- Introduction to Quantitative Finance

Pure Mathematics Courses:
- Abstract Algebra
- Real Analysis

Remember to consult with an academic advisor for course selection and to ensure that you meet all the requirements for your major. Also, note that you cannot double-count a course for two different requirements. For example, Operations Research can only count for either 1 Advanced course or 1 Elective course, but not both. Enjoy your studies!

### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?

### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The process of making a Capstone for graduation involves several steps, which can vary depending on whether you're following the guidelines for a dissertation or creative writing capstone.

For a dissertation-based Capstone:
1. Early meetings with your advisor to set up a regular meeting schedule and expectations for submissions with timelines.
2. At the beginning of the semester, meet with your advisor to discuss and set goals for the project.
3. By the end of the term, submit an end-of-term submission that demonstrates successful progress towards the final Capstone submission and satisfactory completion. This could include:
   - A literature review or annotated bibliography of at least five pages (2,000 words).
   - An introduction.
   - Other materials or documents to be decided upon in consultation with your advisors (e.g., questionnaires).

For a creative writing-based Capstone:
1. Early meetings with your advisor to set up a regular meeting schedule and expectations for submissions with timelines.
2. At the beginning of the semester, meet with your advisor to discuss and set goals for the project.
3. In Capstone II, you will focus more on production, whether it be writing your thesis or realizing a creative project.
4. The end-of-term submission will likely involve demonstrating successful progress towards the final Capstone submission and satisfactory completion. Specific requirements may include:
   - A literature review or annotated bibliography of at least five pages (2,000 words).
   - An introduction.
   - Other materials or documents to be decided upon in consultation with your advisors (e.g., questionnaires).

Remember that the specific requirements and processes can vary, so it's important to consult with your advisors to understand the exact expectations for your Capstone project.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA, you need to achieve a grade point average (GPA) that falls within the range of 90 to 100. This can be influenced by excelling in your courses, maintaining high-quality work, and possibly taking challenging courses that are recognized for their difficulty and rigor. However, it's important to note that GPA alone isn't the only factor considered for honors; other aspects such as research contributions, leadership roles, and extracurricular activities might also play a role. Additionally, achieving an honor pass capstone is a key requirement for graduating with Honor. The exact GPA needed for honors can vary depending on the institution's policies and the distribution of grades among students. Therefore, it's advisable to consult with your advisor or academic department for specific guidance tailored to your situation.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. • I = Incomplete: If a student is unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), a temporary grade of ‘I’ (Incomplete) may be awarded by the faculty until unfinished course requirements are completed. The student has until the date agreed upon with the faculty (not to exceed 6 months from the end of the course) to complete all remaining course work; otherwise, the student will be

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis by completing a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submitting it to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term (16-week term). For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are two types of absences mentioned in the given context: general absences and excused absences due to university-sponsored events/activities. However, it's important to note that the context also mentions specific scenarios like military leave, personal leave, medical leave, and administrative leave of absence, which can be considered as additional types of absences. So, in total, there are six types of absences.
