### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. You can have a leave of absence by completing and submitting the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form along with supporting documents before the last day of class. Fulbright permits students in Good Academic Standing to apply for a leave of absence for one to two terms. However, normally, a student is not permitted to remain on campus during a period of absence from their studies. You must also meet with your Academic Advisor to discuss a plan to complete a degree. If approved, the effective date of the Leave of Absence will be from the date of request submission. Note that if you submit the request after specific weeks into the term, you should be aware of the potential impact on your studies.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is outlined in Fulbright University Vietnam's Code of Academic Integrity. If a case of academic dishonesty is reported, the Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office. An investigation follows, and if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. If mediation is not possible, a panel review is organized by the Registrar's Office with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation becomes the final grade. For cases involving the interpretation of course policies, the Dean’s Office defers to the course syllabus whenever possible, and makes a final ruling otherwise. This process ensures that any violations of academic integrity are addressed thoroughly and fairly.

DISMISSAL: In all circumstances, Fulbright’s goal is to support students in the completion of their degree. However, dismissal from Fulbright may occur if a suspended student does not fulfill the conditions of suspension, if a student’s behavior represents present harm to others in the Fulbright community, or if a student’s academic performance is unsatisfactory to the degree that continued enrollment is deemed unsupportable. Such decisions are never taken likely, and dismissal occurs only in extraordinary circumstances following multiple written warnings, as determined by the Dean’s Office in consultation with appropriate members of faculty and staff.

In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

The policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades are outlined as follows:

1. For core courses, students must repeat the course if they receive a grade of 'F' or any grade below 'C-' for courses counting towards the major or minor.

2. Students may also repeat a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP' for the course, or if they have withdrawn and received a grade of 'W'.

3. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after receiving a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with the student's academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. This request should consider course availability and capacity in the next academic term or year.

4. If a student repeats a course, a higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and will remain on the transcript.

5. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits.

6. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet major requirements.

7. Students should consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.

These policies aim to provide flexibility while maintaining academic standards and integrity.

### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance by allowing them to apply for a medical leave of absence. Students must submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form and the Fulbright Impact Assessment form, along with all medical supporting documents, before the last day of class. The duration of the leave is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar's Office, and the student. The university also considers other forms of exceptional circumstances such as close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties. For excused absences due to university-sponsored events/activities, the faculty or supervising staff can request an Excused Absence form and submit it to the Dean's Office. In cases of emergencies, students are also accommodated, provided they are unable to communicate their condition to the instructor(s). However, indefinite leaves are not permitted. The university encourages instructors to accommodate students as much as possible within the framework of these policies.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]
EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
with the student’s recovery or safety. If a student determines that medical leave would be beneficial, the student must submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form and the Fulbright Impact Assessment form, along with all medical supporting documents, before the last day of class. Voluntary medical leaves are based on the recommendation of a health services professional that verifies the impact on the capability of completing the academic activities, including but not limited to: • Able to attend the class (Yes/No) • Able to do sustained reading, note-taking, and writing (Yes/No) • Able to perform a task requiring intense concentration for 1-2 hours (Yes/No) Leave duration is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar’s Office, and the student. Indefinite leaves are not permitted. 9.3 Administrative Leave of Absence A student may be placed on an administrative leave of absence if he/she has an outstanding student account balance in an enrolled term without informing

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but under specific conditions. They must provide full documentation of its usage, which includes clearly defining the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the specific elements of the project it contributes to. Additionally, they need to specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed, outline how AI will be incorporated, and address ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI. This comprehensive documentation ensures transparency and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. It is important to note that the use of generative AI is subject to Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity. Therefore, students should follow the guidelines and obtain IRB approval if necessary. Failure to comply with these requirements may result in delays or suspension of the project.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]

This comprehensive documentation promotes transparency, oﬀers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. 1.8. The course demonstrates mathematical concepts and hands-on skills required for the algorithms that are typically used in practice. ### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?

You can get support for mental health treatment through various resources mentioned in the document such as the Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services and other projects like the Community Survey on Mental Health Needs and Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes. These resources aim to address mental health needs within the community and provide guidance and information on local services. However, it's important to note that specific support options may vary depending on your location and the particular needs you're addressing. Always consult with a healthcare provider or mental health professional for personalized advice and treatment options. The document does not provide direct contact information or specific service providers, so you would need to follow up on the details provided in the resource guide or other listed projects to find appropriate support in your area.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit for courses you took at another university towards your Fulbright undergraduate degree, you need to follow these steps:

1. **Submit an Application for Credit Transfer**: You should submit an Application for Credit Transfer to the Office of the Registrar. This application requires detailed information about the courses you wish to transfer, including the course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

2. **Provide Required Documentation**: Along with the application, you must provide an official transcript with the seal from the issuing institution. This document should be sent directly to the Office of the Registrar either via email (registrar@fulbright.edu.vn) or through the provided mailing address mentioned in the policy.

3. **Review and Approval Process**: After submission, the Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to review your application and determine whether the credit can be transferred or if an exemption is warranted. The decision will be based on whether the courses meet Fulbright's standards and equivalency requirements.

4. **Wait for Confirmation**: Once the evaluation process is complete, the approved courses will be reflected in your official transcript under the "Transfer Credit" section in the following term.

By following these steps, you can successfully apply for credit transfer towards your Fulbright undergraduate degree. Remember, Fulbright will not evaluate transferable credit prior to acceptance, so ensure you have been accepted into the Fulbright program before initiating this process. Additionally, it's advisable to review the Transfer Credit Policy V1.0 published in the One-Stop portal to get more detailed guidance.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you typically won't need to take physical education courses as part of your graduation requirements. Many institutions offer a waiver or exemption for student athletes from these requirements. You should check with your specific institution's athletic department or academic advisor to confirm the exact process and any additional requirements you might need to meet. This information is usually detailed in your student handbook or available through your institution's policies. Remember, even though physical education courses don't count towards the 128-credit requirement, they still contribute to your overall educational experience and may be important for maintaining your athletic eligibility. Always consult with your advisor to ensure compliance with all institutional policies.

All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, it seems like you are asking about re-registering for dormitory accommodation and whether you would still receive financial support.

From the context given, students who wish to return to Fulbright after withdrawing formally or without permission must reapply for admission and financial aid. Since you are currently a third-year student and have already withdrawn from the dormitory after your first year, you would need to reapply for both dormitory accommodation and financial support.

The process involves submitting an application for admission and financial aid, which would then be reviewed according to the current academic regulations, degree program, and curriculum requirements. Your academic record would remain unchanged upon reinstatement, except under special circumstances decided by the Dean's Office.

However, the context does not provide specific details regarding the availability of dormitory spaces or the financial support process. Therefore, you should contact the relevant offices at Fulbright to inquire about the availability of dormitory spaces and the financial support process for third-year students. They will be able to provide you with more detailed and accurate information based on your specific situation. 

In summary, you would need to reapply for both dormitory accommodation and financial support, but you should contact Fulbright's relevant offices for more detailed information on the availability and process.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

According to the information provided in the context, there are four main ways the university offers support for students experiencing exceptional circumstances:

1. Exceptional medical circumstances, such as hospitalization or incapacitation due to injury, illness, or mental health crisis.
2. Close bereavement involving partners, children, parents, siblings, grandparents, and grandchildren, or housemates and very close friends (with evidence required).
3. Being a victim of a serious crime.
4. Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student.

These are the specific circumstances outlined in the context that the university acknowledges and provides support for. However, it's noted that the reference to "Other reasons. Please specify:" suggests there might be additional unspecified reasons for support, but these are not detailed in the given text. Therefore, based on the provided information, there are four main ways mentioned.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided in the context, here's what you should do:

1. Document your concerns: Keep a detailed record of instances where the professor's delivery did not meet academic standards. This could include specific examples of poor communication, lack of clarity, or inappropriate content.

2. Review the course syllabus: Check if there are any specific policies regarding student feedback or complaints. If the professor has a policy for handling such issues, follow it.

3. Speak to the professor: Before escalating the issue, try to address it directly with the professor. You might want to schedule a meeting to discuss your concerns in a professional manner.

4. File a formal complaint: If the issue persists and you feel uncomfortable addressing it directly with the professor, you can file a formal complaint with the Registrar's Office. Provide them with your documented concerns and any other relevant information.

5. Follow up: After filing a complaint, keep track of the process and follow up as necessary. If the Dean's Office needs more information from you, provide it promptly.

6. Be prepared for mediation: According to the context, if the Deans can mediate, no further action may be required. However, if they cannot mediate, a panel review will be organized for an independent evaluation of the grade.

7. Respect the process: Trust the institution's processes and give them time to investigate and resolve the issue. If the issue is related to the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean's Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible. Otherwise, they will make a final ruling on the matter. 

Remember, it's important to handle the situation professionally and constructively. Good luck!

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

For a third-year student considering a capstone project, it would be advisable to seek advice from the major capstone coordinator. They can provide guidance on whether you should undertake a capstone project given your current academic standing and help you navigate the process. Additionally, they can assist in finding a suitable primary advisor who has expertise relevant to your potential project. If necessary, they can also help identify a secondary advisor at another institution if needed. It's important to consult with the capstone coordinator early in your academic planning to ensure you make an informed decision about your capstone project.

### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

You should contact the Academic Affairs team or Registrar's Office during business hours for assistance with your request for absence and obtaining the official transcript. They can guide you through the process and provide the necessary forms, such as the Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form. Additionally, make sure to summarize the program or activity, provide proof of your attendance, and write a reflection paper as required. Remember to inform the Office of the Registrar upon your return and register for classes using the One-Stop platform for the term you're returning to.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work effectively on your major report, follow these steps:

1. **Executive Summary**: Structure it as follows:
   - What is the problem?
   - What is the purpose of the program?
   - What has been done so far?
   - Your program details.
   - Evaluation findings.
   - Summarize the meaning of your evaluation findings.

2. **Formatting and Referencing**: Ensure that your entire evaluation report is correctly formatted and referenced. Each chapter should start on a new page, and your chapter numbering and Table of Contents should be accurate. Make sure your Reference List and in-text citations align properly, and include any required Appendices, especially the documentation.

3. **Word Limit**: Keep the word count (excluding production documents) under 5000 words. The executive summary should be between 200-250 words.

4. **Public Defense**: Prepare for a public defense of your work, which will be evaluated by a capstone panel of at least three members appointed by the major. This includes a presentation and a Q&A session.

5. **Advisor Meetings**: Plan to meet with your primary advisor at least once a month, initiating these meetings as needed. Your primary advisor should be knowledgeable about your project's disciplinary field and will be the main reviewer of your work.

6. **Capstone Panel Evaluation**: The final scores for your capstone project are computed based on the following weight distribution:
   - Advisor(s): 40%
   - Independent Reviewer: 30%
   - Capstone Panel: 30%

7. **Final Submission**: Convert your Word file into a single PDF document after making all necessary revisions and submitting it for evaluation. Ensure that the score meets the criteria for a Pass grade (70%-89.9%) or Pass with Honor (90%) to receive the appropriate grade. 

By following these steps, you can ensure that your major report is well-prepared, professionally formatted, and effectively communicated to your evaluators and the broader audience.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

You can fill in the requirements of EL in various ways depending on your course selection and major/minor combinations. However, the specific number of ways is not provided in the given context. The context mentions that up to 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass and up to two of those can be counted towards the student's major requirements. It also states that the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Therefore, the number of ways to fulfill the requirements depends on individual course choices and how they align with the major and minor requirements.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement.
